## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / batch reactor ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly a reaction-rate expression for concentration A evolving over time t, which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics in batch systems. Typical relationships are kinetic rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, inhibition, autocatalysis) and sometimes explicitly on t via time-varying rate coefficients (catalyst deactivation, temperature programs, mixing/transport transients).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay/consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of A; surface-limited or saturated reactant regime)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, dilution, radioactive-like kinetics for concentration)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or pseudo-second-order in A)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global order kinetics)
- General production + decay (source-sink): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (net formation with linear loss; chemostat-like or side-loss approximation)
- Relaxation to equilibrium (linear driving force): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to steady-state/equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible/relaxation with nonlinear order: dA_dt = c0 * (c1**c2 - A**c2) (approach to equilibrium with order-like nonlinearity)
- Autocatalytic/logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating production with depletion/limited capacity)
- Inhibited kinetics (self-inhibition): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (rate slows at high A due to inhibition/complexation)
- Time-varying first-order (linear drift in rate coefficient): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (temperature/programmed conditions or slow parameter drift)
- Catalyst deactivation (exponential loss of activity): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant decays with time)
- Transport/mixing transient to a target profile: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) / (1 + c2 * t) (relaxation slows over time due to diffusion boundary growth or mixing transients)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is predominantly negative and proportional to A, it suggests first-order consumption; proportional to A**2 suggests bimolecular/self-reaction behavior.
- A constant (A-independent) term in dA_dt indicates zero-order kinetics (surface saturation, constant-rate feed/withdrawal, or strong saturation in the true mechanism).
- A factor like (c1 - A) implies attraction to a steady state/equilibrium concentration c1; the sign of c0 determines stability (relaxation vs divergence).
- Presence of A*(c1 - A) indicates autocatalysis with self-limitation (sigmoidal time course in A rather than simple exponential).
- A rational slowdown like A/(1 + c*A) indicates inhibition/complexation: increasing A eventually reduces marginal rate increase (sublinear effective order).
- Explicit time dependence in the prefactor (c0 + c1*t) or exp(-c*t) often represents changing conditions (temperature ramps) or catalyst deactivation/aging.
- A rate prefactor that decreases like 1/(1 + c*t) is consistent with diffusion-layer growth or mixing/transport transients where effective mass transfer weakens over time.
- If dA_dt changes sign near a particular A value, that A is a stable/unstable fixed point; locating roots of the fitted rate law identifies steady states.

This has: `A*c0` âœ“, `A*c3*exp(c4*t)` âœ“, `c6*sin(c7*log(A*c8+1)+c9)` - can match `sin(log(A+1))` by setting c7=1, c8=1, c9=0. Extra terms: `A*c1/(A*c2+1)` - set c1=0, `c5` - set c5=0. This works! âœ“

**Candidate 10:** `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*log(A*c4 + 1) + c5 + c6*sin(c7*log(A*c8 + 1) + c9)`

Has extra `c3*log(A*c4+1)` - set c3=0. Has `c5` - set c5=0. Remaining: `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c6*sin(c7*log(A*c8+1)+c9)`. This matches GT! âœ“

All other candidates lack `sin(log(...))`. The GT's `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be represented by combinations of `log`, `exp`, polynomials, rational functions, or `sin(A*c + c)` (which is sin of a linear function, not sin of log). Let me verify candidates with `sin(A*c + c)` like 30, 31, 36, 42, 44, 50 - these have `sin(linear in A)`, not `sin(log(A+1))`, so they cannot match.

For all other candidates (1,2,4-9,11-29,32-49 except 3,10): None contain `sin(log(...))`. Since `sin(log(A+1))` is linearly independent from all combinations of polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, and rational functions, none of these can match.
